/>.net</a></span></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2">
<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Musical artist</div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Azealia Amanda Banks</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;z&#39; in &#39;zoom&#39;">z</span><span title="/iː/: &#39;ee&#39; in &#39;fleece&#39;">iː</span><span title="&#39;l&#39; in &#39;lie&#39;">l</span><span title="/i/: &#39;y&#39; in &#39;happy&#39;">i</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span></span>/</a></span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling">ə-<span style="font-size:90%">ZEE</span>-lee-ə</i></a>; born May 31, 1991) is an American rapper, singer and songwriter. Raised in the <a href="/wiki/Harlem" title="Harlem">Harlem</a> neighborhood of New York City, she began releasing music through <a href="/wiki/Myspace" title="Myspace">Myspace</a> in 2008 before being signed to <a href="/wiki/XL_Recordings" title="XL Recordings">XL Recordings</a> at age 18. She subsequently signed with <a href="/wiki/Interscope_Records" title="Interscope Records">Interscope</a> and <a href="/wiki/Polydor_Records" title="Polydor Records">Polydor Records</a> before separating in 2013. Banks became an independent artist and started her own independent record label, Chaos &amp; Glory Recordings. She is currently signed to <a href="/wiki/Parlophone" title="Parlophone">Parlophone</a> and <a href="/wiki/Warner_Records" title="Warner Records">Warner Records</a>. 
</p><p>Banks's song "<a href="/wiki/212_(song)" title="212 (song)">212</a>" has been listed as one of the best songs of 2011 and one of the defining songs of the decade by music publications, including <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i>. She has since released two mixtapes (<i><a href="/wiki/Fantasea_(mixtape)" title="Fantasea (mixtape)">Fantasea</a></i> in 2012 and <i><a href="/wiki/Slay-Z" title="Slay-Z">Slay-Z</a></i> in 2016), a studio album (<i><a href="/wiki/Broke_with_Expensive_Taste" title="Broke with Expensive Taste">Broke with Expensive Taste</a></i> in 2014), and two extended plays (<i><a href="/wiki/1991_(Azealia_Banks_EP)" title="1991 (Azealia Banks EP)">1991</a></i> in 2012 and <i><a href="/wiki/Icy_Colors_Change" title="Icy Colors Change">Icy Colors Change</a></i> in 2018). In 2017, Banks had her film debut in the musical drama <i><a href="/wiki/Love_Beats_Rhymes" title="Love Beats Rhymes">Love Beats Rhymes</a></i>, portraying the lead character. Banks's works have garnered acclaim from critics, drawing on various sounds including <a href="/wiki/House_(genre)" class="mw-redirect" title="House (genre)">house</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rap" class="mw-redirect" title="Rap">rap</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pop_(genre)" class="mw-redirect" title="Pop (genre)">pop</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electronic_music" title="Electronic music">electronic music</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Avant-garde" title="Avant-garde">avant-garde</a>.
</p><p>Throughout her career, Banks's <a href="/wiki/Social_media" title="Social media">social media</a> presence and outspoken views, especially on <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_the_United_States" title="Politics of the United States">U.S. politics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Race_(human_categorization)" title="Race (human categorization)">race</a>, as well as disputes with other artists,<sup id="cite_ref-:0_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> have attracted significant controversy.<sup id="cite_ref-beefs_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-beefs-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-The_Independent_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Independent-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Complex_(magazine)" class="mw-redirect" title="Complex (magazine)">Complex</a></i> noted in 2014 that "she gets more attention for her public feuds than she does for her music".<sup id="cite_ref-beefs_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-beefs-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Life_and_career">Life and career</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life_and_career_beginnings">Early life and career beginnings</span></h3>
<p>Azealia Amanda Banks was born on May 31, 1991, in New York City's <a href="/wiki/Manhattan" title="Manhattan">Manhattan</a> borough; she was the youngest of three.<sup id="cite_ref-xxlmag22ndbirthday_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xxlmag22ndbirthday-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Her single mother raised her and her two siblings in <a href="/wiki/Harlem" title="Harlem">Harlem</a>, after their father died of <a href="/wiki/Pancreatic_cancer" title="Pancreatic cancer">pancreatic cancer</a> when she was two years old.<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes1_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes1-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Following her father's death, Banks says that her mother "became really abusive—physically and verbally. Like she would hit me and my sisters with baseball bats, bang our heads up against walls, and she would always tell me I was ugly. I remember once she threw out all the food in the fridge, just so we wouldn't have anything to eat." Due to escalating violence, Banks moved out of her mother's home at age 14 to live with her older sister.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At a young age, Banks became interested in musical theater, dancing, acting, and singing. At 16, she starred in a production of the comedy-noir musical <i><a href="/wiki/City_of_Angels_(musical)" title="City of Angels (musical)">City of Angels</a></i>, where she was found by an agent who sent her to auditions for <a href="/wiki/TBS_(U.S._TV_channel)" class="mw-redirect" title="TBS (U.S. TV channel)">TBS</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nickelodeon" title="Nickelodeon">Nickelodeon</a>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Law_%26_Order" title="Law &amp; Order">Law &amp; Order</a></i>, all without success.<sup id="cite_ref-Spin_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spin-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> At this point Banks decided to end her pursuit of an acting career, citing the stiff competition and overall sense of nonfulfillment.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Because of this lack of fulfillment, she began writing rap and <a href="/wiki/Rhythm_and_blues" title="Rhythm and blues">R&amp;B</a> songs as a creative outlet. She never finished high school, instead choosing to follow her dream of becoming a recording artist.<sup id="cite_ref-xxlmag22ndbirthday_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xxlmag22ndbirthday-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Under the moniker Miss Bank$, she released her debut recording, "Gimme a Chance" online on November 9, 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-Spin_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spin-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> The recording was accompanied by the self-produced track "Seventeen", which sampled the <a href="/wiki/Ladytron" title="Ladytron">Ladytron</a> song of the <a href="/wiki/Seventeen_(Ladytron_song)" title="Seventeen (Ladytron song)">same name</a>. Banks sent both tracks to American DJ <a href="/wiki/Diplo_(DJ)" class="mw-redirect" title="Diplo (DJ)">Diplo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Later that year, she signed a <a href="/wiki/Artist_development_deal" title="Artist development deal">development deal</a> with record label <a href="/wiki/XL_Recordings" title="XL Recordings">XL Recordings</a> and began working with producer <a href="/wiki/Richard_Russell_(XL_Recordings)" class="mw-redirect" title="Richard Russell (XL Recordings)">Richard Russell</a> in London, leaving the label later that year due to conflicting ideas.<sup id="cite_ref-so12_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-so12-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-xl_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xl-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2011.E2.80.932012:_1991_and_Fantasea"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2011–2012:_1991_and_Fantasea">2011–2012: <i>1991</i> and <i>Fantasea</i></span></h3>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/1991_(Azealia_Banks_EP)" title="1991 (Azealia Banks EP)">1991 (Azealia Banks EP)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fantasea_(mixtape)" title="Fantasea (mixtape)">Fantasea (mixtape)</a></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1062260506">.mw-parser-output .quotebox{background-color:#F9F9F9;border:1px solid #aaa;box-sizing:border-box;padding:10px;font-size:88%;max-width:100%}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft{margin:.5em 1.4em .8em 0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright{margin:.5em 0 .8em 1.4em}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.centered{overflow:hidden;position:relative;margin:.5em auto .8em auto}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft span,.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright span{font-style:inherit}.mw-parser-output .quotebox>blockquote{margin:0;padding:0;border-left:0;font-family:inherit;font-size:inherit}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-title{background-color:#F9F9F9;text-align:center;font-size:110%;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote>:first-child{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote:last-child>:last-child{margin-bottom:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:before{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" “ ";vertical-align:-45%;line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:after{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" ” ";line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .left-aligned{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .right-aligned{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .center-aligned{text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .quote-title,.mw-parser-output .quotebox .quotebox-quote{display:block}.mw-parser-output .quotebox cite{display:block;font-style:normal}@media screen and (max-width:640px){.mw-parser-output .quotebox{width:100%!important;margin:0 0 .8em!important;float:none!important}}</style><div class="quotebox pullquote floatleft" style="width:30em; ;">
<blockquote class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">
<p>Richard [Russell] was cool, but as soon as I didn't want to use his beats, it got real sour. He wound up calling me "amateur" and the XL interns started talking shit about me. It just got real fucking funny. I was like, "I didn't come here for a date. I came here to cut some fucking records." I got turned off on the music industry and disappeared for a bit. I went into a bit of a depression.
</p>
</blockquote>
<p><cite class="right-aligned" style="">—Banks talking of her departure from XL Recordings<sup id="cite_ref-xl_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xl-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup></cite>
</p>
</div><p> After leaving XL Recordings, Banks dropped the 'Miss Bank$' moniker and formally became Azealia Banks, which preceded a move to <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">Montreal</a>. Using YouTube as a portal, she uploaded several demo tracks, including "L8R" and a cover of "<a href="/wiki/Slow_Hands_(Interpol_song)" title="Slow Hands (Interpol song)">Slow Hands</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Interpol_(band)" title="Interpol (band)">Interpol</a>. After her Canadian <a href="/wiki/Visa_(document)" class="mw-redirect" title="Visa (document)">visa</a> expired, Banks returned to New York, where she sold keychains at a Manhattan jazz club and danced at a <a href="/wiki/Queens" title="Queens">Queens</a> strip club to make ends meet.<sup id="cite_ref-Spin_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spin-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> "That's when I was really depressed", Banks said. "I don't have a manager, I don't have a boyfriend, I don't have any friends, I don't have any money. Here I am working at the strip club, trying not to say the wrong thing and get into fights with these girls who don't give a shit."<sup id="cite_ref-Spin_12-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spin-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In September 2011, Banks released her debut single, "<a href="/wiki/212_(song)" title="212 (song)">212</a>", as a free digital download from her website. It was released officially on December 6, 2011, as the lead single from her <a href="/wiki/Extended_play" title="Extended play">EP</a> <i><a href="/wiki/1991_(Azealia_Banks_EP)" title="1991 (Azealia Banks EP)">1991</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-212release_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212release-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> The track attained moderate European chart success, peaking at #14 in the Netherlands, #12 in the United Kingdom and #7 in Ireland.<sup id="cite_ref-nldchart_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nldchart-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-irlchart_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-irlchart-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ukchart_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ukchart-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Azealia_Banks_Art_Basel_2012.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Azealia_Banks_Art_Basel_2012.jpg/220px-Azealia_Banks_Art_Basel_2012.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Azealia_Banks_Art_Basel_2012.jpg/330px-Azealia_Banks_Art_Basel_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Azealia_Banks_Art_Basel_2012.jpg/440px-Azealia_Banks_Art_Basel_2012.jpg 2x" data-file-width="612" data-file-height="612" /></a><figcaption>Banks performing at the <a href="/wiki/Art_Basel#Art_Basel_in_Miami_Beach" title="Art Basel">Art Basel in Miami Beach</a>, 2012</figcaption></figure><p>Though unsigned at the time, Banks began working with British producer <a href="/wiki/Paul_Epworth" title="Paul Epworth">Paul Epworth</a> on a debut studio album.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> It was announced in December 2011 that she would feature on "<a href="/wiki/Shady_Love" title="Shady Love">Shady Love</a>", a track on American band <a href="/wiki/Scissor_Sisters" title="Scissor Sisters">Scissor Sisters</a>' fourth studio album, <a href="/wiki/Magic_Hour_(Scissor_Sisters_album)" title="Magic Hour (Scissor Sisters album)"><i>Magic Hour</i></a>, though the feature was uncredited. An accompanying video was released in January 2012 following its radio premiere from <a href="/wiki/Annie_Mac" title="Annie Mac">Annie Mac</a> (<a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_1" title="BBC Radio 1">BBC Radio 1</a>) on January 4,<sup id="cite_ref-shadyvideo_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shadyvideo-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> though the single's release was canceled for unconfirmed reasons. Banks released the track "NEEDSUMLUV (SXLND)" online on January 16, 2012, coinciding with what would have been the 33rd birthday of the late singer <a href="/wiki/Aaliyah" title="Aaliyah">Aaliyah</a>, who is sampled on the track.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> A week later saw the emergence of a second track, "Bambi", produced by <a href="/wiki/Paul_Epworth" title="Paul Epworth">Paul Epworth</a> and selected as the soundtrack for a <a href="/wiki/Thierry_Mugler" title="Thierry Mugler">Thierry Mugler</a> fashion show in Paris.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 2012, Banks announced plans to release a <a href="/wiki/Mixtape" title="Mixtape">mixtape</a>—originally titled <i>Fantastic</i>—titled <i><a href="/wiki/Fantasea_(mixtape)" title="Fantasea (mixtape)">Fantasea</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-schedule_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-schedule-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Preceding its release the tracks "Jumanji",<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> "Aquababe",<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> and "Nathan" (featuring rapper <a href="/wiki/Styles_P" title="Styles P">Styles P</a>) were made available online.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> <i>Fantasea</i> was released via Banks's Twitter account on July 11,<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> and was succeeded by the unveiling of her online radio project <i>Kunt.FM</i> the following week.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Banks's first EP, <i><a href="/wiki/1991_(Azealia_Banks_EP)" title="1991 (Azealia Banks EP)">1991</a></i>, was released in the UK on May 28 and in the US the next day.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> The 4-track EP, which includes <a href="/wiki/212_(song)" title="212 (song)"><i>212</i></a>, was not eligible for the <a href="/wiki/UK_Albums_Chart" title="UK Albums Chart"><i>UK Albums</i></a> chart, but the title track charted at #79 on the <a href="/wiki/UK_Singles_Chart" title="UK Singles Chart"><i>UK Singles</i></a> chart.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> It also reached #133 on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200">US 200</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> while reaching #17 on the <a href="/wiki/Top_R%26B/Hip-Hop_Albums" title="Top R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Albums"><i>US R&amp;B/Hip-Hop</i></a> chart,<sup id="cite_ref-R&amp;BAlbums_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-R&amp;BAlbums-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> #12 on the <a href="/wiki/Rap_Albums" class="mw-redirect" title="Rap Albums"><i>US Rap</i></a> chart,<sup id="cite_ref-RapAlbums_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RapAlbums-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> and headin' <a href="/wiki/Top_Heatseekers" class="mw-redirect" title="Top Heatseekers"><i>US Heat</i></a> chart.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> In 2013, <a href="/wiki/1991_(Azealia_Banks_EP)" title="1991 (Azealia Banks EP)"><i>1991</i></a> was certified gold by the <i><a href="/wiki/Australian_Recording_Industry_Association" title="Australian Recording Industry Association">Australian Recording Industry Association</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Banks was scheduled to release her second single, "Esta Noche", from <i>Fantasea</i>, on September 25, 2012, but it was pulled the day of its release due to sampling disputes between Banks and its producer, <a href="/wiki/Munchi_(DJ)" title="Munchi (DJ)">Munchi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> The next month, it was confirmed that Banks had worked with <a href="/wiki/Lady_Gaga" title="Lady Gaga">Lady Gaga</a> on two tracks, "Ratchet" and "Red Flame", on Gaga's third studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Artpop" title="Artpop">Artpop</a></i> (2013), but they did not make the final album cut, and have not been released.<sup id="cite_ref-ladygagakanyewestcollabo_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ladygagakanyewestcollabo-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Banks also revealed that she collaborated with <a href="/wiki/Kanye_West" title="Kanye West">Kanye West</a> on <a href="/wiki/G.O.O.D._Music" class="mw-redirect" title="G.O.O.D. Music">G.O.O.D. Music</a>'s compilation album <i><a href="/wiki/Cruel_Summer_(GOOD_Music_album)" title="Cruel Summer (GOOD Music album)">Cruel Summer</a></i> but that her contributions did not make the final cut.<sup id="cite_ref-ladygagakanyewestcollabo_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ladygagakanyewestcollabo-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> On December 31, 2012, Banks released "BBD", which ultimately appeared on her debut album, <i>Broke with Expensive Taste</i>.
</p>
<h3><span id="2013.E2.80.932016:_Broke_with_Expensive_Taste_and_Slay-Z"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2013–2016:_Broke_with_Expensive_Taste_and_Slay-Z">2013–2016: <i>Broke with Expensive Taste</i> and <i>Slay-Z</i></span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Broke_with_Expensive_Taste" title="Broke with Expensive Taste">Broke with Expensive Taste</a> and <a href="/wiki/Slay-Z" title="Slay-Z">Slay-Z</a></div><figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Life_Ball_2013_-_opening_show_034_Azealia_Banks.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Life_Ball_2013_-_opening_show_034_Azealia_Banks.jpg/220px-Life_Ball_2013_-_opening_show_034_Azealia_Banks.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Life_Ball_2013_-_opening_show_034_Azealia_Banks.jpg/330px-Life_Ball_2013_-_opening_show_034_Azealia_Banks.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Life_Ball_2013_-_opening_show_034_Azealia_Banks.jpg/440px-Life_Ball_2013_-_opening_show_034_Azealia_Banks.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2700" data-file-height="1800" /></a><figcaption>Banks performing at <a href="/wiki/Life_Ball" title="Life Ball">Life Ball</a> 2013</figcaption></figure>
<p>Early in 2012, Banks revealed that her debut album would be called <i><a href="/wiki/Broke_with_Expensive_Taste" title="Broke with Expensive Taste">Broke with Expensive Taste</a></i>, and said it would include contributions from musicians including <a href="/wiki/Toko_Yasuda" title="Toko Yasuda">Toko Yasuda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Theophilus_London" title="Theophilus London">Theophilus London</a>, Kevin Hussein, and <a href="/wiki/Ariel_Pink" title="Ariel Pink">Ariel Pink</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> She initially said the album's lead single would be a track titled "Miss Amor" and that it would be accompanied by a <a href="/wiki/B-side" class="mw-redirect" title="B-side">B-side</a>, "Miss Camaraderie", both produced by <a href="/wiki/Lone_(musician)" title="Lone (musician)">Lone</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> but these plans changed: in January 2013 she announced that the first official single from the album would be "<a href="/wiki/Yung_Rapunxel" title="Yung Rapunxel">Yung Rapunxel</a>", which was released in March 2013 on <a href="/wiki/SoundCloud" title="SoundCloud">SoundCloud</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-yungrapunxelasfirstsingle_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yungrapunxelasfirstsingle-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 2013, Banks announced that the second single from <i>Broke with Expensive Taste</i> would be "<a href="/wiki/ATM_Jam" title="ATM Jam">ATM Jam</a>", featuring <a href="/wiki/Pharrell_Williams" title="Pharrell Williams">Pharrell</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> On June 29, she debuted the song at the <a href="/wiki/Glastonbury_Festival_2013" title="Glastonbury Festival 2013">2013 Glastonbury Festival</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> with New York City radio station <a href="/wiki/WQHT" title="WQHT">Hot 97</a> premiering a clean, shortened version of the studio recording three days later.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> On July 11, the full studio version of "ATM Jam" was released on <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_1" title="BBC Radio 1">BBC Radio 1</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Banks confirmed in November 2013 that "ATM Jam" would not appear on <i>Broke with Expensive Taste</i> due to negative fan feedback and personal disinterest regarding the song.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Azealia_Banks_at_2013_Glastonbury_Festival_(cropped).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Azealia_Banks_at_2013_Glastonbury_Festival_%28cropped%29.jpg/197px-Azealia_Banks_at_2013_Glastonbury_Festival_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="197" height="233" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Azealia_Banks_at_2013_Glastonbury_Festival_%28cropped%29.jpg/296px-Azealia_Banks_at_2013_Glastonbury_Festival_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Azealia_Banks_at_2013_Glastonbury_Festival_%28cropped%29.jpg/394px-Azealia_Banks_at_2013_Glastonbury_Festival_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="824" data-file-height="974" /></a><figcaption>Banks performing at the <a href="/wiki/Glastonbury_Festival_2013" title="Glastonbury Festival 2013">2013 Glastonbury Festival</a></figcaption></figure>
<p>Banks announced in mid-July that after a long battle, she had parted ways with Universal Music Group. She reportedly has possession and the rights to the work she released with Interscope.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> On July 28, 2014, Banks released the official second single from <i>Broke with Expensive Taste</i>, titled "<a href="/wiki/Heavy_Metal_and_Reflective" title="Heavy Metal and Reflective">Heavy Metal and Reflective</a>", on her own label, <i>Azealia Banks Records</i>.
</p><p>Banks surprise-released <i>Broke with Expensive Taste</i> under <a href="/wiki/Prospect_Park_(production_company)" title="Prospect Park (production company)">Prospect Park</a> on iTunes on November 7, 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> The physical album was released on March 3, 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> In 2015, Banks performed at the <a href="/wiki/Coachella_Valley_Music_and_Arts_Festival" class="mw-redirect" title="Coachella Valley Music and Arts Festival">Coachella Valley Music and Arts Festival</a> and posed nude for the April issue of <i><a href="/wiki/Playboy" title="Playboy">Playboy</a></i>, shot by <a href="/wiki/Ellen_von_Unwerth" title="Ellen von Unwerth">Ellen von Unwerth</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> In late 2015, Banks revealed that she was unable to release new music until March 2016,<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> due to the separation from her label, Prospect Park, but as of February 2016 she was officially cleared of her contract and able to release new music.
</p><p>In February 2016, Banks released the single, "<a href="/wiki/The_Big_Big_Beat" title="The Big Big Beat">The Big Big Beat</a>", with its official video uploaded to Vevo in April.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> The song would serve as the lead single to Banks's second mixtape, <i><a href="/wiki/Slay-Z" title="Slay-Z">Slay-Z</a></i>, which was released on March 24, 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> In July 2017, <i>Slay-Z</i> was reissued to iTunes, Spotify, and other online music stores under her independent record label, Chaos &amp; Glory Recordings. The re-issue would include the <a href="/wiki/Lunice" title="Lunice">Lunice</a> collaboration, "<a href="/wiki/Crown_(Azealia_Banks_song)" title="Crown (Azealia Banks song)">Crown</a>", which was released as the project's sole bonus track.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2017.E2.80.93present:_Icy_Colors_Change_and_upcoming_projects"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2017–present:_Icy_Colors_Change_and_upcoming_projects">2017–present: <i>Icy Colors Change</i> and upcoming projects</span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Icy_Colors_Change" title="Icy Colors Change">Icy Colors Change</a></div>
<p>In early 2017, Banks launched her online store, CheapyXO. The site features artist merchandise from Banks as well as original skin care products.<sup id="cite_ref-Spin_12-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spin-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> The site also includes "CheapyXO Radio" which links to a playlist curated by Banks herself. Banks would later relaunch the site in 2020 to include her podcast, <i>Cheapy's Two Cents</i>, as well as, "Botantica XO", which is composed of spiritual items.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Banks announced that her next project will be <i>Fantasea II: The Second Wave</i>, a follow-up to 2012 mixtape <i>Fantasea</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> On June 5, 2017, Banks released the song "<a href="/wiki/Chi_Chi_(Azealia_Banks_song)" title="Chi Chi (Azealia Banks song)">Chi Chi</a>"<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> intended to be the lead single from <i>Business &amp; Pleasure,</i> however, it was later demoted to a stand-alone single.<sup id="cite_ref-facebook_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-facebook-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> On June 26, 2017, Banks released the promotional single, "<a href="/wiki/Escapades_(Azealia_Banks_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Escapades (Azealia Banks song)">Escapades</a>", from the upcoming album <i>Fantasea II: The Second Wave</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> After a yearlong hiatus from touring, Banks returned to New York City to embark on a <a href="/wiki/Azealia_Banks:_North_American_Tour_2017" class="mw-redirect" title="Azealia Banks: North American Tour 2017">North American tour</a> with 20 dates across the U.S. and Canada. The tour began on October 4 in Chicago and concluded on October 31 in San Francisco.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> Banks also performed across Europe in a handful of shows during 2017.
</p><p>It was announced in 2015 that Banks would make her acting debut as the main character in the <a href="/wiki/RZA" title="RZA">RZA</a>-directed musical drama film <i>Coco</i> (now known as <i><a href="/wiki/Love_Beats_Rhymes" title="Love Beats Rhymes">Love Beats Rhymes</a></i>).<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> The film was officially released on December 1, 2017.
</p><p>On January 31, 2018, Banks announced that she had signed a US$1 million record deal with <a href="/wiki/Entertainment_One" title="Entertainment One">Entertainment One</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> On March 9, 2018, she released "Movin' On Up" to iTunes and other streaming platforms as the second promotional single from <i>Fantasea II: The Second Wave</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> The song was previously featured in the 2017 film <i><a href="/wiki/Love_Beats_Rhymes" title="Love Beats Rhymes">Love Beats Rhymes</a></i> which Banks starred in. In March 2018, she announced that the first official single from her forthcoming album would be "<a href="/wiki/Anna_Wintour_(Azealia_Banks_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Anna Wintour (Azealia Banks song)">Anna Wintour</a>". It was released on April 6, 2018, and the official music video for the single was released on May 24, 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> On July 6, a second single, "Treasure Island", was released.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> In November, Banks announced on her <a href="/wiki/Instagram" title="Instagram">Instagram</a> account that she would release the Christmas-themed EP <i><a href="/wiki/Icy_Colors_Change" title="Icy Colors Change">Icy Colors Change</a></i> on December 7. A demo of the title track was released in December 2017. The project was released on December 19 after several delays, with a promotional single, "<a href="/wiki/What_Are_You_Doing_New_Year%27s_Eve" class="mw-redirect" title="What Are You Doing New Year&#39;s Eve">What Are You Doing New Year's Eve</a>?", released on December 13.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> Another promotional single from <i>Fantasea II: The Second Wave</i>, "Playhouse", was released exclusively on <a href="/wiki/SoundCloud" title="SoundCloud">SoundCloud</a> on April 12, 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> Banks first teased the track back in 2016 by playing the entire song on the live streaming app, <a href="/wiki/Periscope_(app)" class="mw-redirect" title="Periscope (app)">Periscope</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Banks separated from <a href="/wiki/Entertainment_One_Music" class="mw-redirect" title="Entertainment One Music">eOne Music</a> in 2019. Consequently, she announced in May of that year that she had been working on a project called <i>Yung Rapunxel: Pt. II</i>. The title references Banks's debut single off <i><a href="/wiki/Broke_with_Expensive_Taste" title="Broke with Expensive Taste">Broke with Expensive Taste</a>,</i> "<a href="/wiki/Yung_Rapunxel" title="Yung Rapunxel">Yung Rapunxel</a>". It was released through SoundCloud on September 11, 2019, before later being taken down.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On December 16, 2019, Banks released the promotional singles "Count Contessa" and "Pyrex Princess" on various streaming platforms. "Pyrex Princess" is a song from <i>Business &amp; Pleasure</i>, previously released on August 22, 2018, before being taken down. "Count Contessa" was previously published on SoundCloud in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> A music video for "Count Contessa", directed by Rony Alwin and shot in Bali, Indonesia, was previously released on December 8, 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Throughout the first quarter of 2020, Banks debuted her podcast <i>Cheapy's Two Cents</i> and released multiple promotional singles, including "Slow Hands", an <a href="/wiki/Interpol_(band)" title="Interpol (band)">Interpol</a> cover previously uploaded in 2012,<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> as well as "Salchichón" being produced by frequent collaborator Onyx.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> Additionally, Banks released multiple tracks exclusively on her SoundCloud, such as "Diamond Nova", which previously served as the B-side to her 2013 single "<a href="/wiki/ATM_Jam" title="ATM Jam">ATM Jam</a>", featuring and produced by <a href="/wiki/Pharrell" class="mw-redirect" title="Pharrell">Pharrell</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> as well as the Spanglish single, "Nirvana".<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On June 9, 2020, Banks released the lead single<sup id="cite_ref-facebook_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-facebook-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> from her as-yet-unreleased album <i>Business &amp; Pleasure</i><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> titled "<a href="/wiki/Black_Madonna_(Azealia_Banks_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Black Madonna (Azealia Banks song)">Black Madonna</a>" featuring producer <a href="/wiki/Lex_Luger_(musician)" class="mw-redirect" title="Lex Luger (musician)">Lex Luger</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> On December 23, 2020, she released the promotional single "Mamma Mia" on all platforms, where it was previously released on her SoundCloud account since April 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> Banks released the single "Six Flags" featuring Slim Dollars on January 7, 2021.
</p><p>On July 7, 2021, Banks released the single "Fuck Him All Night". A perfume of the same name was launched months later.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> She also announced that she was under new management.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Banks began teasing a track titled "New Bottega" in August 2022.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> On November 9, she announced that she had officially signed to <a href="/wiki/Parlophone" title="Parlophone">Parlophone</a> Records, under <a href="/wiki/Warner_Music_Group" title="Warner Music Group">Warner Music Group</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> In January 2023, she posted an Instagram Story stating that she had left Parlophone and announced that she would instead release "New Bottega" independently.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> After several delays, "New Bottega" was released by the Australian dance music label <a href="/wiki/Sweat_It_Out_(record_label)" title="Sweat It Out (record label)">Sweat It Out</a> on March 10, 2023, as a collaboration between Australian house producer <a href="/wiki/Torren_Foot" title="Torren Foot">Torren Foot</a> and Banks.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> But the following May, Banks said she had not authorized the release and criticized Torren Foot's rework of the song, which she called "a piss poor remix of [her] master track". She also criticized Sweat It Out for marketing "New Bottega" as a dance recording instead of a hip hop song.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Artistry">Artistry</span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1134653256">.mw-parser-output .side-box{margin:4px 0;box-sizing:border-box;border:1px solid #aaa;font-size:88%;line-height:1.25em;background-color:#f9f9f9;display:flow-root}.mw-parser-output .side-box-abovebelow,.mw-parser-output .side-box-text{padding:0.25em 0.9em}.mw-parser-output .side-box-image{padding:2px 0 2px 0.9em;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .side-box-imageright{padding:2px 0.9em 2px 0;text-align:center}@media(min-width:500px){.mw-parser-output .side-box-flex{display:flex;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .side-box-text{flex:1}}@media(min-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .side-box{width:238px}.mw-parser-output .side-box-right{clear:right;float:right;margin-left:1em}.mw-parser-output .side-box-left{margin-right:1em}}</style><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1096940132">.mw-parser-output .listen .side-box-text{line-height:1.1em}.mw-parser-output .listen-plain{border:none;background:transparent}.mw-parser-output .listen-embedded{width:100%;margin:0;border-width:1px 0 0 0;background:transparent}.mw-parser-output .listen-header{padding:2px}.mw-parser-output .listen-embedded .listen-header{padding:2px 0}.mw-parser-output .listen-file-header{padding:4px 0}.mw-parser-output .listen .description{padding-top:2px}.mw-parser-output .listen .mw-tmh-player{max-width:100%}@media(max-width:719px){.mw-parser-output .listen{clear:both}}@media(min-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .listen:not(.listen-noimage){width:320px}.mw-parser-output .listen-left{overflow:visible;float:left}.mw-parser-output .listen-center{float:none;margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto}}</style><div class="side-box side-box-left listen noprint listen-left"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1126788409">.mw-parser-output .plainlist ol,.mw-parser-output .plainlist ul{line-height:inherit;list-style:none;margin:0;padding:0}.mw-parser-output .plainlist ol li,.mw-parser-output .plainlist ul li{margin-bottom:0}</style>
<div class="side-box-flex">
<div class="side-box-image"><figure class="mw-halign-center" typeof="mw:File"><span><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/50px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="50" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/75px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/100px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="160" data-file-height="160" /></span><figcaption></figcaption></figure></div>
<div class="side-box-text plainlist"><div class="haudio">
<div class="listen-file-header"><a href="/wiki/File:212_by_Azealia_Banks.ogg" title="File:212 by Azealia Banks.ogg">"212"</a></div>
<div><span typeof="mw:File"><span><audio id="mwe_player_0" controls="" preload="none" class="mw-file-element" width="232" style="width:232px;" data-durationhint="21" data-mwtitle="212_by_Azealia_Banks.ogg" data-mwprovider="local"><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/7/7f/212_by_Azealia_Banks.ogg" type="audio/ogg; codecs=&quot;vorbis&quot;" data-title="Original Ogg file (65 kbps)" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-width="0" data-height="0" /><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/transcoded/7/7f/212_by_Azealia_Banks.ogg/212_by_Azealia_Banks.ogg.mp3" type="audio/mpeg" data-title="MP3" data-shorttitle="MP3" data-transcodekey="mp3" data-width="0" data-height="0" /><track src="/w/api.php?action=timedtext&amp;title=File%3A212_by_Azealia_Banks.ogg&amp;lang=en&amp;trackformat=vtt" kind="subtitles" type="text/vtt" srclang="en" label="English ‪(en)‬" data-dir="ltr" /></audio></span></span></div>
<div class="description">The 2011 song features numerous vocal shifts, as well as lyrics containing <a href="/wiki/Word_play" title="Word play">word play</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alliteration" title="Alliteration">alliteration</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Assonance" title="Assonance">assonance</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div></div>
<div class="side-box-abovebelow"><hr /><i class="selfreference">Problems playing this file? See <a href="/wiki/Help:Media" title="Help:Media">media help</a>.</i></div>
</div>
<p>Banks has said she admires American recording artists <a href="/wiki/Beyonc%C3%A9" title="Beyoncé">Beyoncé</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aaliyah" title="Aaliyah">Aaliyah</a>, calling the former "the queen of everything. She's the most remarkable performer and musician. And this is just my humble opinion, but I just think she's better than everyone else making music right now."<sup id="cite_ref-rollingstone_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rollingstone-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> Banks is inspired by, and has drawn directly upon, black gay culture, such as the film <i><a href="/wiki/Paris_Is_Burning_(film)" title="Paris Is Burning (film)">Paris Is Burning</a></i>, in her music.<sup id="cite_ref-Moore_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Moore-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/AllMusic" title="AllMusic">AllMusic</a> characterizes Banks as "a stylish vocalist who combines <a href="/wiki/Hardcore_hip-hop" class="mw-redirect" title="Hardcore hip-hop">hardcore hip-hop</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indie_pop" title="Indie pop">indie pop</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Dance_music" title="Dance music">dance music</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> Meanwhile, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s John Robinson considered Banks's style "an appealing blend of <a href="/wiki/Missy_Elliott" title="Missy Elliott">Missy Elliott</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dance-pop" title="Dance-pop">dance-pop</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> In regards to her musical style, Banks has frequently been noted for the use of profanity in many of her songs, particularly her <a href="/wiki/Reappropriation" title="Reappropriation">reclamation</a> of the word "cunt",<sup id="cite_ref-independent_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-independent-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-samcam_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-samcam-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-guardianmarch_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardianmarch-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> examples including her debut single "<a href="/wiki/212_(song)" title="212 (song)">212</a>", in which she uses the word more than ten times, or other songs such as <a href="/wiki/Fantasea_(mixtape)" title="Fantasea (mixtape)">"Fierce"</a>, in which she refers to herself as the "cunt queen".<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> Banks attributes this to her upbringing in Harlem, saying, "...I'm from Harlem. I went to art school; I grew up with the cunts. And that term doesn't come from me! People think I invented it, but I didn't. To be cunty is to be feminine and to be, like, aware of yourself. Nobody's fucking with that inner strength and delicateness. The cunts, the gay men, adore that. My friends would say, 'Oh you need to cunt it up! You're being too <a href="/wiki/Banjee" title="Banjee">banjee</a>.' Banjee means unrefined and rough. You need your cunts: they fix your hair for you and do your makeup. They give you confidence and give you life."<sup id="cite_ref-rollingstone_97-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rollingstone-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> She is also known for her often fast-paced rapping, or "<a href="/wiki/Flow_(rapping)" class="mw-redirect" title="Flow (rapping)">flow</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-guardianmarch_103-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardianmarch-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> In a review of Banks's debut <a href="/wiki/Extended_play" title="Extended play">EP</a> <a href="/wiki/1991_(Azealia_Banks_EP)" title="1991 (Azealia Banks EP)"><i>1991</i></a>, Chris Dart of <i><a href="/wiki/Exclaim!" title="Exclaim!">Exclaim!</a></i> found Banks's rapping speed "remarkable", commenting that she "manages a feat that takes most rappers the better part of a career to master: the perfect marriage of bangin', club-friendly beats and smart, crisply delivered lyrics".<sup id="cite_ref-Dart_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dart-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Since writing "212", Banks has adopted an alter ego, "Yung Rapunxel". This alter ego was adapted from Banks calling herself <a href="/wiki/Rapunzel" title="Rapunzel">Rapunzel</a> due to a long <a href="/wiki/Artificial_hair_integrations" title="Artificial hair integrations">weave</a> she wore while working at <a href="/wiki/Starbucks" title="Starbucks">Starbucks</a> as a teenager. Banks discussed this with <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> saying, "Yung Rapunxel is that girl who pisses people off but doesn't really mean to. She's actually a sweetheart! But people are so taken aback that she's so herself; she's not even trying to be unique or different. She literally just lives in her head; she does what she wants to do. So, the lipstick is here for someone who is happy to be themself."<sup id="cite_ref-rollingstone_97-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rollingstone-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span></h2>
<p>In October 2019, Banks announced that she would perform under the name Azilka (<a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>: <span lang="ru">Азилька</span>) during her tour in the <a href="/wiki/Former_Soviet_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Former Soviet Union">former Soviet Union</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-azilka_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-azilka-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On August 8, 2020, Banks announced that she intended to end her life by <a href="/wiki/Euthanasia" title="Euthanasia">euthanasia</a> and document the process on film.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In February 2021, Banks publicly announced her engagement to American artist <a href="/wiki/Ryder_Ripps" title="Ryder Ripps">Ryder Ripps</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> They made an audio <a href="/wiki/Sex_tape" class="mw-redirect" title="Sex tape">sex tape</a> and sold it using <a href="/wiki/Non-fungible_token" title="Non-fungible token">NFT</a>, which was then up for resale for $260 million.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> In March, Banks announced the end of the relationship.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span></h3>
<p>In July 2016, Banks admitted to lightening her skin due to skin blemishes from her birth control and defended the process of <a href="/wiki/Skin_whitening" title="Skin whitening">skin bleaching</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> In December 2016, she revealed that she had had a <a href="/wiki/Miscarriage" title="Miscarriage">miscarriage</a> and asked her fans for advice and support.<sup id="cite_ref-Havens_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Havens-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/BuzzFeed_News" title="BuzzFeed News">BuzzFeed News</a></i> wrote Banks "has been frank about her own mental health issues".<sup id="cite_ref-Abdelmahmoud_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abdelmahmoud-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> In 2020, during a plea deal in Manhattan Court to avoid prison time, she was ordered to seek mental health treatment.<sup id="cite_ref-mental_health_tx_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mental_health_tx-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> The British magazine <i><a href="/wiki/Gal-dem" title="Gal-dem">gal-dem</a></i> reported that she has <a href="/wiki/Bipolar_disorder" title="Bipolar disorder">bipolar disorder</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bipolar_diagnosis_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bipolar_diagnosis-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sexuality_and_views_on_the_LGBT_community">Sexuality and views on the LGBT community</span></h3>
<p>Banks identifies as <a href="/wiki/Bisexual" class="mw-redirect" title="Bisexual">bisexual</a>. During the few instances where she has discussed her sexuality with the press, she has expressed dissatisfaction with society's labeling of others based on <a href="/wiki/Sexual_orientation" title="Sexual orientation">sexual orientation</a>. In an interview with <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i>, she said, "I'm not trying to be, like, the bisexual, lesbian rapper. I don't live on other people's terms."<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes1_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes1-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>Banks has been accused of both homophobia and transphobia, with <i><a href="/wiki/Out_(magazine)" title="Out (magazine)">Out</a></i> editors calling her a bully to the LGBT community rather than an ally.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> In 2015, she used language that <i><a href="/wiki/PinkNews" title="PinkNews">PinkNews</a></i> called homophobic when she called a flight attendant a "fucking faggot" during what it described as an "in-flight meltdown".<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> Later that month, Banks posted what <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i> called a "Twitter tirade" against the LGBT community when she tweeted, "LGBT community are like the gay white <a href="/wiki/Ku_Klux_Klan" title="Ku Klux Klan">KKK</a>'s. Get some pink hoods and unicorns and rally down rodeo drive... If I am to be a part of an LGBT community I want to be in it with people who aren't so weak or so easily moved ya know."<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> In 2020, she said gay men were "appropriating horse culture" by using harnesses, <a href="/wiki/Ketamine" title="Ketamine">ketamine</a>, and sexual lubricant.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> In 2021, she said <a href="/wiki/Trans_women" class="mw-redirect" title="Trans women">trans women</a> are "just gay boys on hormones using male aggression to force their ways into <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_spaces" class="mw-redirect" title="Women&#39;s spaces">women's spaces</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> In 2023, she argued that state funding for other healthcare issues should take precedence over funding for <a href="/wiki/Gender-affirming_surgery" title="Gender-affirming surgery">gender-affirming surgery</a>, which she compared to "cosmetic surgery".<sup id="cite_ref-FaderDeSantis2023_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FaderDeSantis2023-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_views">Political views</span></h3>
<p>Banks is known for publicly speaking out on African-American civil rights issues, with a commentator at <i><a href="/wiki/Splice_Today" class="mw-redirect" title="Splice Today">Splice Today</a></i> describing her as having "that hot New York temper where she will pop off if you cross her the wrong way".<sup id="cite_ref-Moore_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Moore-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Independent14_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Independent14-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> In December 2014, she called for over $100 trillion to be paid to African Americans as <a href="/wiki/Reparations_for_slavery_debate_in_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Reparations for slavery debate in the United States">financial reparations for the enslavement of their ancestors</a>, citing U.S. reparations to Native American communities and the German reparations to Jewish survivors of <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust" title="The Holocaust">the Holocaust</a> as precedents.<sup id="cite_ref-Independent14_123-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Independent14-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NME14_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NME14-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> On Twitter, she urged young African Americans to take an interest in such issues, adding, "We are the children of the people who perished in the name of modern capitalism and we deserve a piece of that fucking pie".<sup id="cite_ref-Independent14_123-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Independent14-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NME14_124-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NME14-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> She added that reparations could be used to improve educational prospects for black Americans.<sup id="cite_ref-Independent14_123-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Independent14-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2016, Banks took to Twitter to express her endorsement of <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump_presidential_campaign,_2016" class="mw-redirect" title="Donald Trump presidential campaign, 2016">2016 presidential campaign</a>, clarifying that "I have no hope for America ... I think Donald Trump is evil like America is evil and in order for America to keep up with itself it needs him ... politicians are inherently evil, I trust the one who is most transparent."<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> She retracted her endorsement of Trump in October 2016, posting on Facebook: "I made a major mistake endorsing toupey-toupee. Women's rights are important and we must protect them."<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> Nonetheless, after Trump won the presidency, she posted, "He is my fucking hero right now. I am elated."<sup id="cite_ref-Thorpe_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thorpe-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2022, Banks posted an Instagram story repeatedly chastising <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2022_Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine" class="mw-redirect" title="2022 Russian invasion of Ukraine">2022 Russian invasion of the country</a>. She claimed, unsubstantiated, that Ukraine's president <a href="/wiki/Volodymyr_Zelenskyy" title="Volodymyr Zelenskyy">Volodymyr Zelenskyy</a> prevented <a href="/wiki/2022_Ukrainian_refugee_crisis#Racial_discrimination" class="mw-redirect" title="2022 Ukrainian refugee crisis">African exchange students from leaving the country</a>. She also claimed without evidence that Ukraine was using its embassies in African countries to recruit mercenaries to fight in Ukraine. Banks said that Zelenskyy was trying to provoke a global nuclear war and urged Ukraine to surrender.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> In a previous Instagram story from April 1, she had praised Russia's president <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a>, saying that she "really fucking love[s]" him and calling him her "favorite <a href="/wiki/Supervillain" title="Supervillain">super villain</a> ever".<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Banks moved from Los Angeles to Miami in 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> In January 2023, she said she did so because she had become disillusioned with the politics of Los Angeles and that she felt "way safer" in Florida.<sup id="cite_ref-GuardianDeSantis2023_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GuardianDeSantis2023-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> She also praised Florida's governor <a href="/wiki/Ron_DeSantis" title="Ron DeSantis">Ron DeSantis</a>, whom she called "focused on the basic shit" and "practical about a lot of things".<sup id="cite_ref-FaderDeSantis2023_122-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FaderDeSantis2023-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GuardianDeSantis2023_132-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GuardianDeSantis2023-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Disputes_and_controversies">Disputes and controversies</span></h2>
<p>Banks has developed a reputation for disputes with several public figures on <a href="/wiki/Social_media" title="Social media">social media</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-The_Independent_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Independent-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> particularly Twitter, with <i><a href="/wiki/Complex_(magazine)" class="mw-redirect" title="Complex (magazine)">Complex</a></i> noting that "she gets more attention for her public feuds than she does for her music".<sup id="cite_ref-beefs_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-beefs-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:0_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Banks has been involved in altercations with crew and passengers aboard commercial flights, resulting in her being removed from airliners, and she has accused some foreign airlines of racism against her.<sup id="cite_ref-Sweden_flight_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sweden_flight-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> She also denounced "racists" in Israel and Australia and said she would never return to either country.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 2016, Banks posted what several media outlets described as a racist and homophobic rant<sup id="cite_ref-ToddBBC_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ToddBBC-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sieczkowski_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sieczkowski-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> against <a href="/wiki/Zayn_Malik" title="Zayn Malik">Zayn Malik</a> on Twitter, later targeting young actress <a href="/wiki/Skai_Jackson" title="Skai Jackson">Skai Jackson</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-sieczkowski_138-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sieczkowski-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> As a result, Banks was dropped by her UK booking agency and an upcoming hip-hop festival, and her Twitter account was suspended.<sup id="cite_ref-ToddBBC_137-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ToddBBC-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> Later Twitter accounts were created then suspended, most recently in 2022.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2016, Banks posted a series of videos on <a href="/wiki/Instagram" title="Instagram">Instagram</a> detailing her cleanup of a closet in her apartment where she claims to have been practicing <a href="/wiki/Witchcraft" title="Witchcraft">witchcraft</a>. She admitted to practicing "three years worth of <a href="/wiki/Witchcraft_in_Latin_America" title="Witchcraft in Latin America">brujeria</a>". The video appeared to show dried blood, feathers, and the <a href="/wiki/Carrion" title="Carrion">carrion</a> of dead chickens.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> In January 2021, she received criticism after posting a video on Instagram of her digging up and cooking her dead pet cat. She later said in an interview that she did not eat the cat and exhumed it for <a href="/wiki/Taxidermy" title="Taxidermy">taxidermizing</a> purposes.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In January 2019, Banks posted xenophobic remarks about Irish people after performing in Ireland, in which she used ethnic slurs and mocked the <a href="/wiki/Great_Famine_(Ireland)" title="Great Famine (Ireland)">Great Famine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> That August, she posted xenophobic remarks about Swedish people after performing in Sweden, adding that she "would really love to see someone bomb the shit out of this place".<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
